Violations of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor punishable only by a fine of
up to one thousand dollars ($1,000.00). (Ord. 2009-12-09, 12-9-2009)
CHAPTER 5
TOBACCO PRODUCTS AND ELECTRONIC CIGARETTES
SECTION:
2-5-1: Purpose And Intent
2-5-2: Definitions
2-5-3: Prohibited Acts
2-5-4: Required Signage To Be Posted; Identification Required
2-5-5: Penalties, Enforcement And Defenses
2-5-1: PURPOSE AND INTENT:
The purpose and intent of this chapter is to protect individuals under the age
of eighteen (18) from the hazards of nicotine addiction and the dangers of
ingesting products with no regulatory oversight as to their purity, contents,
and potential negative health impacts. (Ord. 2015-5-13, 5-13-2015)
2-5-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter:
DELIVERY SALE: To distribute electronic cigarettes to a consumer in a state
where either: a) the individual submits the order for such sale by means of a
telephonic or other method of voice transmission, data transfer via computer
networks, including the internet and other online services, or facsimile, or
the mail; or b) the electronic cigarettes are delivered by use of the mail or a
delivery service.
DELIVERY SERVICE: Any person who is engaged in the commercial delivery of
letters, packages or other containers.
DISTRIBUTE: To give, deliver, sell, offer to give, offer to deliver, offer to
sell, market, distribute or cause any person to do the same or hire any person
to do the same.
ELECTRONIC CIGARETTE OR E-CIGARETTE: Any device that can provide an inhaled
dose of nicotine by delivering a vaporized solution. "Electronic cigarette" or
"e-cigarette" includes each component of an electronic cigarette including, but
not limited to, liquid nicotine.
LIQUID NICOTINE: Any liquid product composed either in whole or in part of
nicotine, propylene glycol and/or other similar substances and manufactured for
use with an e-cigarette to be converted into a gas for inhaling.
PERSON: Any natural person, individual, corporation, limited liability company,
unincorporated association, proprietorship, firm, partnership, joint venture,
joint stock association, or other entity or business of any kind.
PHOTOGRAPHIC IDENTIFICATION: State, district, territorial, possession,
provincial, national or other equivalent government driver's license,
identification card or military card, in all cases bearing a photograph and a
date of birth, or a valid passport.
TOBACCO PRODUCT: Any substance that contains tobacco including, but not limited
to, cigarettes, cigars, pipes, snuff, smoking tobacco, tobacco papers or
smokeless tobacco.
VENDING MACHINE: Any mechanical, electronic or other similar device which, upon
the insertion of tokens, money or any other form of payment, dispenses tobacco
products or electronic cigarettes.
VENDOR ASSISTED: Any sale or distribution in which the customer has no access
to the product except through the assistance of the person distributing,
selling or offering the product. (Ord. 2015-5-13, 5-13-2015)
2-5-3: PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   No person shall distribute tobacco products, e-cigarettes, their
components, or samples thereof to any person under eighteen (18) years of age.
   B.   Except as provided for under subsection E of this section, no person
shall distribute tobacco products or e-cigarettes, their components or samples
thereof in any manner that does not require an in person transaction in a
retail store to help prevent redemption of such merchandise by a person under
eighteen (18) years of age.
   C.   Unless more than seventy five percent (75%) of the retail store is
related to the sale of ordinary tobacco products or e-cigarettes, and all
minors are excluded from the establishment with prominent warnings at all
doorways, no person shall distribute tobacco products or e-cigarettes, their
components or samples thereof in any manner that does not require vendor
assistance.
   D.   No person shall distribute tobacco products or e-cigarettes, their
components or samples thereof through a vending machine unless the vending
machine is located fully within the retail store establishment, at least ten
feet (10') from all entryways and exits and all minors are excluded from the
establishment with prominent warnings at all doorways.
   E.   No person shall engage in the delivery sale or delivery service of
tobacco products or e-cigarettes, their components or samples thereof in any
manner without first verifying any recipient's or purchaser's address and that
such recipient or purchaser is eighteen (18) years of age or older.
   F.   No person shall distribute tobacco products or e-cigarettes, their
components or samples thereof in any format other than the approved and
original packaging by the manufacturer.
   G.   No person under the age of eighteen (18) shall purchase, attempt to
purchase, possess, or obtain tobacco products, e-cigarettes or their
components. This prohibition does not apply to activities or enforcement
actions under the control of a city, state, or federal law enforcement
authority. (Ord. 2015-5-13, 5-13-2015)
2-5-4: REQUIRED SIGNAGE TO BE POSTED; IDENTIFICATION REQUIRED:
   A.   Any person distributing tobacco products or e-cigarettes, their
components or samples thereof, shall display within the retail establishment a
printed sign, posted so that it is clearly visible to anyone therein. The sign
must be in contrasting colors and at least 20-point type and must read
substantially as follows:
IF YOU ARE UNDER 18, YOU COULD BE SUBJECT TO PENALTY FOR PURCHASING TOBACCO
PRODUCTS, E-CIGARETTES OR RELATED DEVICES OR THEIR COMPONENTS. THE SALE OF
TOBACCO PRODUCTS, E-CIGARETTES OR RELATED DEVICES OR THEIR COMPONENTS TO
PERSONS UNDER THE AGE OF 18 IS STRICTLY PROHIBITED. PHOTO ID REQUIRED.
(Ord. 2015-5-13, 5-13-2015)
2-5-5: PENALTIES, ENFORCEMENT AND DEFENSES:
   A.   Violation of any provision of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor. Each
transaction is a new and separate violation.
   B.   It is a defense to a prosecution for violation of this chapter relating
to age when the person distributing reasonably relied on an officially issued
photographic identification showing the purchaser or recipient was at least
eighteen (18) years old.
   C.   The failure of a person to request and examine photographic
identification from any person under eighteen (18) years of age prior to the
distribution of tobacco products or e-cigarettes or related devices or
components thereof to such person shall be construed against the person and
form a conclusive basis for that person's violation of this chapter.
   D.   It is a defense to subsection
2-5-3D of this chapter if the person demonstrates to the satisfaction of the
building official that it is architecturally impracticable for the vending
machine to be located not less than ten feet (10') from all entrance and exit
ways. (Ord. 2015-5-13, 5-13-2015)
TITLE 3
PUBLIC HEALTH AND SAFETY
CHAPTER 1
GARBAGE AND REFUSE
SECTION:
3-1-1: Compulsory Use Of System; Exceptions
3-1-2: Definitions
3-1-3: Refuse Collection And Disposal
3-1-4: Storage Of Garbage And Refuse
3-1-5: Refuse Accumulation Unlawful
3-1-6: Violation; Penalty
3-1-1: COMPULSORY USE OF SYSTEM; EXCEPTIONS:
Every owner and occupant of premises within the prescribed limits of the City
must use the refuse collection and disposal system herein provided and shall
deposit or cause to be deposited in accordance with the regulations all rubbish
and garbage, which is accumulated on such premises; provided, that in areas of
the City where the collection of garbage and refuse on the schedule hereinafter
set forth, would be impracticable, the City Council may issue a special permit
altering the time and extent of collection. (Ord. 10, 12-12-1972)
3-1-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this Chapter, terms used herein are defined as follows:
COLLECTOR: The person holding a license or contract with the City or employed
by the City and thereby authorized and designated by the City to collect,
handle, transport and dispose of refuse and wastes.
GARBAGE: Includes all putrescible waste, except sewage and body waste,
including waste accumulated of animal, food or vegetable matter, and including
waste that attends the preparation, use, cooking, dealing in or storing of
meat, fish, fowl, fruit and vegetable, and shall include all of such wastes or
accumulations of vegetable matter of residences, restaurants, hotels and places
where food is prepared for human consumption.
The term "garbage" shall not include recognized industrial by-products.
INSPECTOR: The authorized employee or employees of the City or some individual
designated by the City Council as having the duty of enforcement of this
Chapter.
OWNER OR OCCUPANT: May be used interchangeably, and shall mean every person in
possession, occupancy, charge or control of any dwelling, flat, rooming house
or any eating place, shop, place of business, manufacturing or business
establishment where garbage or other refuse is created or accumulated.
PERSON: Any person, firm, partnership, association, institute or corporation
and a plural as well as a singular.
REFUSE: Solid wastes, including garbage and rubbish.
RUBBISH: Refuse other than garbage (tin cans, bottles, ashes, paper,
pasteboard, cardboard, or wooden boxes, leaves, weeds and cuttings from lawns
and gardens and other waste materials produced in normal course of doing
business or every day living).
The term "rubbish" shall not include recognized industrial by-products.
WASTE: Unwanted solids, liquids or gaseous materials. (Ord. 10, 12-12-1972)
3-1-3: REFUSE COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL:
   A.   Licensing Or Contracting:
      1.   License Or Contract Required: There is hereby established a system
of refuse collection, transportation and disposal. It shall be unlawful for any
person to engage in the business of collecting, transporting, hauling or
conveying any refuse over the streets or alleys of the City, or to dump or
dispose of the same, unless and until such person is licensed therefor, or has
a contract therefor as an authorized representative of the City.
      2.   Authority To License Or Contract: The Mayor and City Council is the
sole authority to license, contract or perform all services pertaining to all
sanitary collection and disposal under this Chapter.
   B.   Collection Schedule: Collectors shall collect rubbish and garbage from
each customer at least once a week or as deemed necessary as provided by the
rules and regulations of the City Council.
   C.   Collection Fees And Rates:
      1.   Fees And Rates Established: Fees and rates for the collection of
garbage and refuse shall be set by rules and regulations of the City. (Ord. 10,
12-12-1972)
         a.   The fees for the collections at single-family residences shall be
five dollars ($5.00) per month, which may be changed by resolution of the City
Council. (Ord. 10, 12-12-1972; amd. 1999 Code)
         b.   The fees for business houses or multiple residences shall be set
by negotiation and contract between the City and the business.
Provided, that where the enforcement of the provisions of this Chapter will
work a financial hardship, or where the amount of refuse and garbage is of such
small amounts as to not warrant the collection of the full charges as herein
provided, the Mayor and City Council may issue a special permit altering the
provisions of this Chapter.
      2.   Bills For Service; Delinquencies: Sanitary service fees shall be
carried on the water bill, and the same shall be paid with the water bill, and
the Water Department is authorized to discontinue services to any premises if
the entire water and garbage fee shall not be paid, said charges to become
delinquent as provided for water charges and shall be subject to the same
penalties provided in the water ordinance.
   D.   Privately Hauling Garbage: Any person may haul their own garbage in
watertight containers. (Ord. 10, 12-12-1972)
3-1-4: STORAGE OF GARBAGE AND REFUSE:
   A.   Containers: It shall be the duty of every owner or occupant of any
place where garbage or rubbish is created or accumulated to at all times keep
or cause to be kept portable appurtenances consisting of metal or other
approved type of container for the deposit therein of rubbish and garbage, and
except as otherwise provided, to deposit or cause to be deposited all rubbish
and garbage therefrom.
      1.   Container Specifications: Such containers shall not be more than
thirty two (32) gallons' capacity and limited to fifty (50) pounds in weight,
when filled. The containers shall not be less than twenty eight (28) gauge
metal or the equivalent, and be hotdipped after fabrication to ensure
nonleaking cans or a can that is guaranteed by the manufacturing processes.
      2.   Watertight With Lid: All such containers shall be watertight, not
easily corrodible, rodent- and flyproof, and shall be equipped with handles and
a close fitting lid. Such lid shall not be removed except when necessary to
place garbage and rubbish in such container or to take the same therefrom.
Whenever garbage or rubbish is placed therein or taken therefrom, such lid
shall be replaced by the person placing or taking therefrom such garbage or
rubbish.
      3.   Sanitary Condition: Containers shall be kept in sanitary condition,
with the inside and outside thereof washed at such times as to keep the same
free and clean of all accumulating grease and decomposing material and so that
no odor nuisance shall exist.
      4.   Placement Of Containers: All garbage or refuse cans shall be kept in
a place accessible to the collector; provided, that in the case of isolated
dwellings or places of business or where reasonable access cannot be had by a
truck, the cans may be kept in such places as may be agreed upon by the owner
and collector, or at such place as may be designated by the Inspector;
provided, further, that whereas there is no alley entrance, such cans shall be
placed on the street curb on collection day.
   B.   Rubbish; Special Handling: Rubbish consisting only of cardboard, or
wooden boxes, leaves, weeds and cuttings from shrubs and gardens may be kept
separately without depositing in such containers; providing, that both
material, such as leaves shall be in a can, box, sack or receptacle for ease of
loading. (Ord. 10, 12-12-1972)
3-1-5: REFUSE ACCUMULATION UNLAWFUL:
It shall be unlawful for any person to permit or to suffer to accumulate in or
about any yard, lot, place or premises, or upon any street, alley or sidewalk
adjacent to such lot, yard, place or premises owned or occupied by such person,
any garbage or refuse so as to cause such yard, lot, premises, street, alley or
sidewalk adjacent thereto, to remain in such a condition as to cause or create
a nuisance or offensive odor or atmosphere or rodents harborage or thereby to
be or to become or cause or create, a public nuisance, within the City limits.
(Ord. 10, 12-12-1972)
3-1-6: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
   A.   Violation: It shall be unlawful and a violation of this Chapter for any
person to throw into or leave on any public thoroughfare or any public place or
on the premises owned by him or on the premises of another, any garbage or
rubbish except in containers as herein specified. (Ord. 10, 12-12-1972)
   B.   Penalty: Any person violating any of the provisions this Chapter shall
be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to
penalty as provided in Section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 10, 12-12-1972; amd. 1999 Code)
CHAPTER 2
NUISANCES
SECTION:
3-2-1: Nuisances Prohibited
3-2-2: Nuisances Enumerated
3-2-3: Violation
3-2-1: NUISANCES PROHIBITED:
Whatever is dangerous or offensive to human life or health, and whatever
renders soil, air, water or food for humans impure or unwholesome are hereby
declared to be nuisances. (1935 Code § 108)
3-2-2: NUISANCES ENUMERATED:
   A.   Offensive Stench: It shall be unlawful for any person to permit any
offensive stench to arise from any premises belonging to him or under his
control in the City, and if any such condition shall exist, the City police may
notify said person to abate same within twelve (12) hours, and if such person
shall fail so to do, said police may enter upon said premises and abate such
condition at the expense of such person. (1935 Code § 107; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-
1967)
   B.   Contaminated Foods: If shall be unlawful for any person to produce or
offer for sale for human consumption, any food, meats, confectionery or drinks
that are impure or dangerous to human life or health or that are kept or
produced under insanitary conditions. (1935 Code § 109; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
   C.   Expectorating In Public: It shall be unlawful for any person to spit
upon or throw any chewed tobacco upon the sidewalks or the floor of any public
building in the City. (1935 Code § 64; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
3-2-3: VIOLATION:
Any person who permits a nuisance to exist in the City, or refuses to abate the
same after notice so to do, is hereby declared to be guilty of a misdemeanor.
(1935 Code § 108; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
CHAPTER 3
NOISE
SECTION:
3-3-1: Authority And Purpose
3-3-2: Excessive Noise Prohibited
3-3-3: Excessive Noise From Vehicle Speakers And Radios, Sound Trucks And
Similar Devices Prohibited
3-3-4: Disturbing The Peace
3-3-5: Dynamic Braking Devices Prohibited
3-3-6: Penalty
3-3-1: AUTHORITY AND PURPOSE:
This chapter is adopted pursuant to the authority granted by Idaho Code section
50-302 to provide for the safety and promote the health, morals, peace, order,
comfort, and convenience of the inhabitants of Franklin City, and to create a
more peaceful and healthful environment within Franklin City. (Ord. 2001-1, 9-
12-2001)
3-3-2: EXCESSIVE NOISE PROHIBITED:
Noise which due to its volume, its duration, or its location disturbs, injures
or endangers the comfort, repose, health, peace, or safety of persons not
voluntary listeners thereto is hereby declared to be excessive and inimical to
the welfare of the citizens of Franklin City. It is unlawful for any person to
make, continue, or cause to be made, or allow to be made on any premises or any
public place or public right of way from any radio, CD player, tape player,
musical instrument, phonograph, or sound amplifier or similar device, any
excessive, loud, unnecessary or unusual noise. Specifically prohibited is the
playing, using, operating, or permitting to be played, used or operated, any
device for playing, producing, or reproducing sound at a louder volume than is
necessary for the hearing of persons who are voluntary listeners on the
premises, or in the building, room, or chamber in which the sound is being
played, produced, or reproduced. Provided, however, that persons engaged in
school related or sports related promotional activities, lawful parades and
community events shall be exempt from the provisions of this chapter for the
duration of the activity. (Ord. 2001-1, 9-12-2001)
3-3-3: EXCESSIVE NOISE FROM VEHICLE SPEAKERS AND RADIOS, SOUND TRUCKS AND
SIMILAR DEVICES PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful to use, operate, or permit to be used, played, or operated,
radios, CD players, tape players, phonographs, vehicle stereo systems, and
similar devices mounted in or on a vehicle loudly enough to disturb the peace,
quiet or comfort of persons who are involuntarily subjected to the sound who
are on or in premises other than the vehicles. Sounds louder than necessary for
the hearing of persons in the vehicle are hereby deemed excessive. Provided,
however, that emergency vehicles and persons engaged in school related or
sports related promotional activities, lawful parades, and community events
shall be exempt from the provisions of this chapter for the duration of the
activity. (Ord. 2001-1, 9-12-2001)
3-3-4: DISTURBING THE PEACE:
It is unlawful for any person to:
   A.   Wilfully or maliciously or intentionally or unnecessarily disturb the
peace and quiet of another by loud or unusual noises or by indecent or
offensive conduct;
   B.   Engage in prolonged shouting, yelling, hooting, whistling, singing, or
playing of musical instruments loud enough to disturb the peace, quiet, and
comfort of persons who are involuntarily subjected to such noise, particularly,
but not limited to, between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and seven
o'clock (7:00) A.M.; provided, however, that persons engaged in school related
or sports related promotional activities, lawful parades, and community events
shall be exempt from the provisions of this chapter for the duration of the
activity. The brief celebratory display of noisemaking at twelve o'clock (12:
00) midnight on New Year's Eve or other official holidays shall not be
considered a violation of this chapter;
   C.   Engage in construction/repair of buildings, including site excavation
and grading, between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and six o'clock (6:
00) A.M., except in case of urgent necessity in the interest of public health
and safety and with the permission of the building official;
   D.   Engage in the use of chain saws and/other woodcutting equipment, or
gasoline or electric powered lawn care equipment between the hours of ten
o'clock (10:00) P.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. in any residential area,
regardless of the underlying zoning district. (Ord. 2001-1, 9-12-2001)
3-3-5: DYNAMIC BRAKING DEVICES PROHIBITED:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person or entity to operate any motor
vehicle with a dynamic braking device engaged within the city of Franklin,
Idaho.
   B.   "Dynamic Braking Device" is defined as a device used primarily on
trucks for the conversion of the engine from an internal combustion to air
compressor for the purpose of braking. Dynamic braking device is also commonly
referred to as a "Jacobs Brake", "Engine Brake" or "Compression Brake". (Ord.
2001-1, 9-12-2001)
3-3-6: PENALTY:
Any person convicted of violation of this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor
and is punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. Each day a violation continues shall be considered a
separate offense. (Ord. 2001-1, 9-12-2001)
CHAPTER 4
SOLID FUEL HEATING APPLIANCES
SECTION:
3-4-1: Authority And Purpose
3-4-2: Definitions
3-4-3: Air Quality Designations And Alert Criteria
3-4-4: Public Notification
3-4-5: Burning Solid Fuel Or Refuse
3-4-6: Solid Fuel Heating Appliance Restrictions And Permits
3-4-7: Exemptions From Restrictions
3-4-8: Minimum Standards For Clean Burning Appliances
3-4-9: Penalty
3-4-1: AUTHORITY AND PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is protect air quality resources vital to the
public health, safety, and welfare of the city of Franklin by controlling
emissions from solid fuel and refuse burning. (Ord. 2012-9-12, 9-12-2012)
3-4-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms, phrases, words, and
derivations all have the meanings given herein. The word "shall" is always
mandatory and not merely directive.
AIR POLLUTION: The presence in the outdoor atmosphere of any contaminate or
combinations thereof in such quality or of such nature and duration and under
such conditions as would be injurious to human health or welfare, to plant or
animal life, or to property, to interfere unreasonably with the enjoyment of
life or property.
BUILDING: Any structure, dwelling, office, industrial plant, garage or barn,
whether publicly or privately owned or any other structure as defined by the
international building code.
BURN DOWN: That period of time following an air pollution alert required for
the cessation of combustion within solid fuel heating appliances or any other
outdoor fires or burning or incineration included within this chapter.
CLEAN BURNING APPLIANCE: A solid fuel heating appliance that has been certified
as clean burning by the United States environmental protection agency (EPA).
FIREPLACE: A residential solid fuel burning device with an air to fuel ratio of
greater than thirty (30) which is a permanent structural feature of a building.
A fireplace is made up of a concealed masonry or metal flue and a masonry or
metal firebox enclosed in decorative masonry or other building materials. A
residential solid fuel burning device which is freestanding or which is
installed into an existing "fireplace" opening is not included in this
definition.
HEAT OUTPUT: The British thermal unit (BTU) per hour output of a solid fuel
heating appliance.
OPEN BURNING: For the purposes of this chapter, the combustion of any material
not contained in a heating appliance. Also for the purposes of this chapter,
the use of a fireplace is considered open burning.
PARTICULATE MATTER (PM10/PM2.5): Any gasborne particles resulting from
incomplete combustion, consisting predominantly, but not exclusively, of carbon
and other combustible matter.
PERSON: Any individual, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company,
organization or governmental entity.
REFUSE: All solid waste, garbage, and rubbish, including, but not limited to,
cardboard, plastic, rubber, styrofoam, petroleum products, foodstuff, Christmas
trees, yard debris or chemically treated wood.
SOLE SOURCE: One or more solid fuel heating devices which constitute the only
source of heat in a building for the purpose of space heating. No solid fuel
heating device(s) shall be the sole source of heat if the building is equipped
with a permanently installed furnace or heating system designed to heat the
building that is connected or unconnected from its energy source, utilizing
oil, natural gas, electricity or propane.
SOLID FUEL: Any form of untreated wood, coal, pressed logs, and pellet fuel.
SOLID FUEL HEATING APPLIANCE: An enclosed device designed for solid fuel
combustion that meets all of the following criteria:
   A.   An air to fuel ratio averaging less than thirty five to one (35:1);
   B.   Firebox volume less than twenty (20) cubic feet;
   C.   Minimum burn rate less than five kilograms (5 kg) per hour; and
   D.   Maximum weight of less than eight hundred kilograms (800 kg). (Ord.
2012-9-12, 9-12-2012)
3-4-3: AIR QUALITY DESIGNATIONS AND ALERT CRITERIA:
   A.   The quality of the city's air shall be determined by monitoring
pollutant levels in and/or around the city with equipment and methods approved
and provided by DEQ at its expense.
   B.   The quality of the city's air shall be designated by DEQ according to
the following table (as may be amended from time to time by the EPA):
      AIR QUALITY INDEX (AQI)
 
Designations                   AQI
Good                              0 - 50
Moderate                          51 - 100
Unhealthy for sensitive groups    101 - 150
Unhealthy                         151 - 200
Very unhealthy                    201 - 300
Hazardous                         301 - 500
 
   C.   All wood burning, including, but not limited to, within a solid fuel
heating appliance designed for wood fuel (commonly known as a "wood stove") or
open fireplace, is prohibited whenever the DEQ forecasts an AQI of seventy five
(75) or greater or forecasts air stagnation conditions will continue for at
least twenty four (24) hours.
   D.   No person shall allow, suffer, cause or permit any open burning of any
kind (see IDAPA 58.01.01.600 - 623) whenever DEQ forecasts an AQI of seventy
five (75) or greater or forecasts air stagnation conditions will continue for
at least twenty four (24) hours. (Ord. 2012-9-12, 9-12-2012)
3-4-4: PUBLIC NOTIFICATION:
Whenever air pollution alert conditions are met, local print and news media,
local officials, the police and fire departments, and city officials will be
notified. In addition DEQ will post information on the DEQ website and the air
quality hotline. (Ord. 2012-9-12, 9-12-2012)
3-4-5: BURNING SOLID FUEL OR REFUSE:
   A.   No person shall cause or allow refuse or coal to be burned in a solid
fuel heating appliance designed for wood fuel commonly known as a "wood stove".
   B.   No person shall cause or allow a wood stove to be operated contrary to
the design, specifications and manufacturer's instructions.
   C.   Notwithstanding the provisions of any section of this chapter, no
person shall allow, suffer, cause, or permit the burning of materials which
emit toxic contaminants or large volumes of smoke, particulate or odors deemed
a public nuisance; such prohibited materials consist of, but are not limited
to, the following: garbage, tires or any other rubber materials, plastics,
heavy petroleum products, dead animals or parts thereof, treated lumber, tree
stumps, trash, wet or green vegetation, trade waste, commercial waste, roofing
materials or any other asphaltic materials, drywall, sheetrock, tarpaper, floor
underlayment, insulation, chemicals, household garbage, motor vehicles or parts
thereof whether junked or not, insulated wire, pathogenic wastes, hazardous
wastes, etc.
   D.   No person shall operate a residential solid fuel burning device or
fireplace if the visible emissions exceed twenty percent (20%) opacity as
measured by EPA method 9, except as follows:
      1.   During an initial fifteen (15) minute startup period, or
      2.   During refueling operations which may not exceed a fifteen (15)
minute period in any three (3) hour period.
   E.   Notwithstanding the provisions of any section of this chapter, no
person shall allow, suffer, cause or permit the burning of any materials when
the AQI as forecasted by the DEQ reaches seventy five (75) or higher for any
air pollutant within the Cache Valley airshed. (Ord. 2012-9-12, 9-12-2012)
3-4-6: SOLID FUEL HEATING APPLIANCE RESTRICTIONS AND PERMITS:
   A.   From the effective date hereof, no person may sell or offer for sale
within the city any solid fuel heating appliance which is not listed and
certified by the EPA as a clean burning appliance.
   B.   No person shall install any solid fuel heating appliance in any new or
existing building without first having obtained a permit to do so from the
city. In order for such a permit to be granted, all such appliances shall be
listed and certified by the EPA as clean burning appliances. Installations
shall be in accordance with the fire code and manufacturer's instructions.
   C.   From the effective date hereof, no person shall construct, or attempt
to construct, any building for which a solid fuel burning appliance will be the
sole source of heat. (Ord. 2012-9-12, 9-12-2012)
3-4-7: EXEMPTIONS FROM RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   All solid fuel burning appliances classified by the EPA as a clean
burning appliance may be operated during an air quality alert.
   B.   A three (3) hour burn down period shall be allowed for solid fuel
heating appliances or fireplaces whose operation was commenced prior to the air
quality alert.
   C.   The city may grant exemptions from this chapter if it is determined
that:
      1.   A solid fuel heating appliance is the sole source of heat for the
structure in which is situated; or
      2.   Using alternative heating would cause an unreasonable economic
hardship.
   D.   Any building constructed after the effective date hereof shall not be
eligible for an exemption under subsections C1 and C2 of this section. (Ord.
2012-9-12, 9-12-2012)
3-4-8: MINIMUM STANDARDS FOR CLEAN BURNING APPLIANCES:
   A.   Appliances shall meet the requirements of the code of federal
regulations title 40, part 60, subpart AAA, "standards of performance for new
residential wood heaters". (Ord. 2012-9-12, 9-12-2012)
3-4-9: PENALTY:
A violation of any of the provisions of this chapter shall constitute a
misdemeanor punishable by a fine up to one thousand dollars ($1,000.00). (Ord.
2012-9-12, 9-12-2012)
TITLE 4
POLICE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
ANIMAL CONTROL
SECTION:
4-1-1: Cruelty To Animals
4-1-2: Animals At Large
4-1-3: Breeding Animals In Public
4-1-4: Sanitary Conditions
4-1-5: City Pound
4-1-6: Poundmaster
4-1-7: Impoundment Procedure
4-1-8: Exceptions From Provisions
4-1-1: CRUELTY TO ANIMALS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to torture, cruelly beat, ill-treat or
inflict pain upon any animal unnecessarily within the City limits, or to place
out any poison either upon their own or any other premises for the purpose of
killing any domestic animals of another. It shall be unlawful to fail to
properly feed and water any domestic animals, or to tie any domestic animals
upon the public streets or in any public place for more than five (5) hours
without food and water. (1935 Code § 41; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
4-1-2: ANIMALS AT LARGE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to permit any horses, cows or cattle of any
kind, sheep, pigs, goats, chickens or poultry of any kind to run at large upon
the public streets, or upon any public grounds or to trespass upon the property
of another. Any person driving any animals through the streets of the City
shall have same under control, and shall proceed with the same without delay to
their destination and shall keep same off public sidewalks, and shall be liable
for any damage they may do in passing through the City, either to public or
private property. (1935 Code § 44; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
4-1-3: BREEDING ANIMALS IN PUBLIC:
It shall be unlawful to stand any animal for breeding service within sight of
the public. (1935 Code § 50)
4-1-4: SANITARY CONDITIONS:
   A.   Location Of Animal Corrals: It shall be unlawful for any person to keep
any corral for horses, cattle or sheep, or any pigsty, within fifty feet (50')
of any sidewalk, or any inhabited house or public building within the City.
(1935 Code § 103; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
   B.   Removal Of Manure: It shall be unlawful for any person to keep any
horses, cattle, sheep, pigs or chickens in any corral, pigsty or chicken house
in the City, unless he shall, before May 1 of each year, remove all manure or
excrement of said livestock from said places, and either spread the same upon
his lands and plow the same under or remove the same from the City limits.
(1935 Code § 104; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
   C.   Dead Animals: It shall be unlawful for any person to permit any dead
animals or poultry to remain on his premises for more than twenty four (24)
hours without either burying same or removing the same outside the City limits
and burying same, and such animals when buried shall be covered by not less
than two feet (2') of earth. (1935 Code § 105; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
4-1-5: CITY POUND:
The Mayor, with the consent of the Council, shall select a suitable enclosure,
and equip the same for use as a City pound for the safekeeping of estrays
running at large within the limits of the City. (1935 Code § 84; amd. Ord. 1,
8-1-1967; 1999 Code)
4-1-6: POUNDMASTER:
   A.   Appointment; Term; Compensation: The Mayor, with the consent of the
Council, shall select a suitable person to act as poundmaster, and such person
shall have the power of a police officer of the City, be under the supervision
of a City designated officer, hold office during the pleasure of said Council,
and receive such compensation for his services as the Council may by resolution
fix. (1935 Code § 85; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967; 1999 Code)
   B.   Duties: It shall be the duty of said poundmaster to take charge of the
City pound and to keep the same in repair, to feed and properly care for any
estrays impounded in the same, to report all estrays to the City Clerk within
twenty four (24) hours of the impounding of the same, to advertise and sell all
unclaimed estrays according to the provisions hereof, and to do all things
under the direction of the Mayor necessary to carry out the intent of this
Chapter. He shall not release to any person any animals impounded in the City
pound, except upon order of the City Clerk. (1935 Code § 86; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-
1967; 1999 Code)
4-1-7: IMPOUNDMENT PROCEDURE:
   A.   Impoundment: It shall be unlawful for any cattle, horses, mules, asses,
sheep, goats, hogs or any other livestock to run at large upon the streets,
alleys or public grounds in the City at any time, and such animals found
running at large shall be considered as estrays, and it shall be the duty of
the poundmaster to take any such animals and to impound the same in the City
pound. (1935 Code § 87; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
   B.   Interference With Poundmaster Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any
person to take any such animals from the custody of the poundmaster after he
has seized the same as estrays and is driving them to the City pound without
his consent, or to take any such animals from the City pound without first
paying the charge for taking up, or costs incurred against such animals
hereunder. (1935 Code § 88; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967; 1999 Code)
   C.   Notice Of Impoundment:
      1.   If the owner of any animal is known and resides in the City, the
poundmaster shall notify such owner in person or in writing within twenty four
(24) hours of the impounding of such animal found running at large within the
limits of the City, and if the known owner of such animal is not a resident of
the City, then the poundmaster shall send notice of the impounding of such
animal to such owner, by registered mail, within twenty four (24) hours of the
impounding of the same.
      2.   If the owner of such animal so impounded is unknown, the poundmaster
shall send a description of such animal, giving its breed, sex, marks, brands
and any distinguishing marks thereon to the Bureau of Registration of the State
Department of Agriculture, at Boise, Idaho, with any necessary fee for
searching the records of ownership, with a request that the owner's name and
address be furnished. He shall give notice of the impounding of said animal
with charges therefor to the owner of said animal, by registered mail, within
twenty four (24) hours of the receipt of such information. (1935 Code § 91;
amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967; 1999 Code)
   D.   Impounding Fees: The owner of any animals seized or impounded as
estrays hereunder shall be required to pay to the City Clerk as a penalty and
as costs for the taking up and keep of any such estrays, a sum to be determined
by resolution by the City Council per head for any cattle, horses, mules or
asses taken up hereunder; and a sum to be determined by resolution by the City
Council per day per head for any major part of a day for the feeding of any
such animals while in custody; and a sum to be determined by resolution by the
City Council per day per head for the taking up and impounding of any sheep,
goats or hogs; and a sum to be determined by resolution by the City Council per
day or part of a day per head for the feeding of any such animals until
claimed. Such persons shall also pay all costs incurred herein. (1935 Code §
89; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967; 1999 Code)
   E.   City Clerk To Keep Records: It shall be the duty of the City Clerk to
keep the City pound book, and register therein the name and description of all
estrays impounded hereunder, the date of their impounding, the date of their
release, the charges assessed and collected against each animal, the amount
received from the sale of all estrays, and the costs and expenses of each sale.
(1935 Code § 90; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
   F.   Disposition Of Unclaimed Animal:
      1.   Notification Of Sale: If the owner of any animal impounded cannot be
found, or if the known owner makes no claim for same or refuses to pay the
charges incurred for the impounding, care of or expense incurred in impounding
or caring for said animal so impounded hereunder, within five (5) days after
being notified of the impounding thereof, then the poundmaster shall advertise
said animal for sale, by posting notice of the time and place of sale, and as
full and accurate a description as possible of the animal to be sold, giving
the approximate age as near as possible, kin, sex, weight, brands and
distinguishing marks of said animal, in three (3) public places in the City,
and publishing the same in the official City newspaper, for not less than two
(2) issues next preceding said sale, and by sending a copy of said notice of
sale to the owner, if known, by registered mail. Such notice shall be posted
and published for not less than ten (10) days nor more than fifteen (15) days
before the date of sale, from the date of posting or first publication of the
notice, and if said animals are not claimed and all costs incurred on account
of them paid before said sale, the same shall be sold at public auction by the
poundmaster to the highest bidder for cash. (1935 Code § 92; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-
1967; amd. 1999 Code)
      2.   Disposition Of Monies: All monies received from the sale of
impounded animals unclaimed shall be turned over by the poundmaster to the City
Clerk, and by him delivered to the City Treasurer. All expenses incurred for
the impounding, keeping, search for owner, advertising or selling of such
animals shall be first paid out of such receipts, and the balance remaining, if
any, shall be placed in a separate fund, and held therein for six (6) months
after such sale, during which time the owner of any animal so sold may appear
and prove his ownership of any animal so sold, and be entitled to receive any
such balance remaining above such costs. All monies unclaimed at the end of
such period shall be placed in the General Fund of the City. (1935 Code § 93;
amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
4-1-8: EXCEPTIONS FROM PROVISIONS:
Nothing contained in this Chapter shall be construed as prohibiting the driving
of animals or stock, while under the supervision or control of a competent
person, through the streets of the City. (1935 Code § 94; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-
1967)
ARTICLE A. DOGS
SECTION:
4-1A-1: Definitions
4-1A-2: License Required
4-1A-3: Kennel Licenses
4-1A-4: Running At Large Or Committing Nuisance
4-1A-5: Animal Control Officer
4-1A-6: Interference With Animal Control Officer
4-1A-7: Impoundment
4-1A-8: Dogs Showing Rabies Symptoms Or Biting Any Person
4-1A-9: Vicious Animals
4-1A-10: Penalties
4-1A-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this article, unless the context otherwise indicates:
ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER: The person or persons designated to enforce this
article.
AT LARGE: Off the premises of the owner and not on a leash or under voice
control of the owner.
COMMERCIAL KENNEL: One wherein the owner or keeper of dogs shall derive monies
from the boarding, breeding, training, treating, or handling of dogs.
DOG: Animal of the canine family, both male and female.
NUISANCE: A dog that damages, defiles, soils or defecates on private property
other than the owner's, or on public walks and recreation areas unless such
waste is immediately removed and properly disposed of by the owner; causes
unsanitary, dangerous or offensive conditions; causes a disturbance by
excessive or continuous barking or other noise making; or chases vehicles, or
molests, attacks, or interferes with persons or other domestic animals on
public property.
OWNER: Any person or persons, firm, association, or corporation owning,
keeping, or harboring a dog.
UNLICENSED DOG: Means and includes any dog not bearing a license issued by the
City for the current year. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990)
4-1A-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall own, keep, or harbor any dog over the age of four (4) months
within the City without paying a license fee as provided in this article, and
obtaining a license for said dog from the City.
   A.   Application For License:
      1.   Application for a license shall be made by the owner before the last
day of January each year, or within thirty (30) days of obtaining an unlicensed
dog over the age of four (4) months, or within thirty (30) days of a dog
turning four (4) months of age.
      2.   Written application for a dog license shall be made to the City
Clerk and shall include the name, address, and telephone number of the owner,
and the name, breed, color, age, and sex of the dog.
      3.   It shall be unlawful for anyone to make a false statement in said
application for said license.
   B.   Term Of License: A license issued shall be effective until December 31
of the year in which issued; provided, that if purchased in 1990, it shall be
effective until December 31, 1991. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990)
   C.   Fee:
      1.   A license shall be issued by the City after payment by the owner of
a fee of fifteen dollars ($15.00) for each neutered or spayed dog and twenty
dollars ($20.00) for each unneutered or unspayed dog. Owners who fail to obtain
a license by the time set forth herein shall be subject to an additional
delinquent fee of ten dollars ($10.00). (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990; amd. per
Council motion 12-1999; Ord., 1-10-2007; Res. 2016-8-31, 8-31-2016, eff. 10-1-
2016)
      2.   License fees shall be waived for dogs serving the blind or deaf. All
other licensing provisions shall apply.
   D.   Tag And Collar:
      1.   Upon payment of the license fee, the City Clerk shall issue to the
owner a metallic tag for each dog so licensed. The tag shall be changed every
year, and shall have stamped thereon the year for which it is issued. Every
owner shall be required to provide each dog with a collar to which the license
tag must be affixed and shall see that the collar and tag are constantly worn.
In case a dog tag is lost or destroyed, a duplicate will be issued by the City
Clerk upon payment of fifty cents ($0.50) for such duplicate.
      2.   Dog tags shall not be transferable from one dog to another and no
refunds shall be made after a tag has been issued.
   E.   Record Kept: The City Clerk shall keep a record of all licenses issued
under the terms of this article.
   F.   Temporary License: When any dog already licensed by another
municipality shall be temporarily in the City for a period of less than thirty
(30) days, the owner or person having charge of the dog may obtain a temporary
license at no cost. A license tag shall be issued with each license, and such
tag shall be securely attached to a substantial, durable collar that the dog
shall wear at all times. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990)
4-1A-3: KENNEL LICENSES:
It shall be unlawful to keep, maintain, harbor or possess upon the premises of
any one household more than two (2) dogs over the age of four (4) months unless
the owner or person in charge thereof shall have obtained a kennel license.
(Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990)
   A.   Noncommercial License; Fees:
      1.   Application for a noncommercial kennel license shall be made to the
City Clerk and must be accompanied by the written consent to such noncommercial
kennel by at least seventy five percent (75%) of all persons in possession of
the premises within one hundred feet (100') of the boundary lines of the
premises upon which said noncommercial kennel is to be maintained, and
accompanied by a deposit of a license fee of five dollars ($5.00) for the first
three (3) dogs and one dollar ($1.00) for each dog over that number, which
deposit shall be returned to the applicant if the license is not finally
issued. The license shall be in force until December 31 of the year in which
issued. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990; amd. Res. 2016-8-31, 8-31-2016, eff. 10-1-
2016)
      2.   The issuance of a noncommercial kennel license shall not obviate the
necessity of obtaining an individual dog license for each dog.
      3.   Noncommercial licenses shall not be transferable. Whenever additions
are made to the number of dogs for which a kennel license has been issued, the
licensee shall within three (3) working days report to the Clerk and pay the
required license fee. Whenever puppies are born, such puppies shall not be
counted as additions until four (4) months old.
   B.   Commercial License: No commercial kennels shall be allowed within the
City. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990)
4-1A-4: RUNNING AT LARGE OR COMMITTING NUISANCE:
   A.   Prohibited; Exceptions: It shall be unlawful for any owner to allow or
permit any dog, whether licensed or not, to be or remain upon the streets of
the City or a public place in the City, or upon the premises of another without
the consent of the person in possession of such other premises, unless:
      1.   Such dog be in the charge of a person and controlled by a leash not
exceeding fifteen feet (15') in length, or such dog be in the charge of an
owner and under voice command of the owner, or unless;
      2.   Such dog be confined in a motor vehicle.
   B.   Penalties: Persons found in violation of subsection A of this section,
as above set forth, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and punished as follows:
(Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990)
      1.   First Offense: A fine of seventy dollars ($70.00) shall be assessed
for the first offense within any continuous twelve (12) month period. (Ord.
1990-2, 11-13-1990; amd. 1999 Code; Ord., 1-10-2007; Res. 2016-8-31, 8-31-2016,
eff. 10-1-2016)
      2.   Second Offense: A fine of one hundred dollars ($100.00) shall be
assessed for the second offense within any continuous twelve (12) month period.
(Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990; amd. Ord., 1-10-2007; Res. 2016-8-31, 8-31-2016, eff.
10-1-2016)
      3.   Third Offense: A fine of one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) shall
be assessed for the third offense and for each other offense above three (3)
within any continuous twelve (12) month period. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990; amd.
Res. 2016-8-31, 8-31-2016, eff. 10-1-2016)
      4.   Additional To Fees: Such fines shall be in addition to license fees,
if unlicensed, and a daily care fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) per day if the
dog has been impounded by the City. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990; amd. Ord., 1-10-
2007; Res. 2016-8-31, 8-31-2016, eff. 10-1-2016)
      5.   Failure To Pay: All license fees, fines, and impound fees shall be
paid to the City Clerk. Failure to pay the same within ten (10) days shall
result in a citation being issued to the owner for the violation and the same
shall be heard in a court of competent jurisdiction. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990)
4-1A-5: ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER:
The Mayor, with the approval of the City Council, may appoint an animal control
officer to enforce and carry out the duties and obligations as provided in this
article. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990)
4-1A-6: INTERFERENCE WITH ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER:
It shall be unlawful and punishable as a misdemeanor for any person to evade or
attempt to evade paying the fee for claiming an impounded dog, or to interfere
with the animal control officer in performance of his duties. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-
13-1990)
4-1A-7: IMPOUNDMENT:
When a dog is found running at large or creating a nuisance, the animal control
officer or his designee shall notify the owner of the dog of such violation, or
if the owner is not known or cannot be contacted, shall seize and impound the
dog.
   A.   Disposition Of Dog:
      1.   The animal control officer or his designee may dispose of any
impounded dog after five (5) or more days have elapsed following notice of
impoundment.
      2.   After a period of five (5) days, the animal control officer or his
designee may dispose of the dog by: a) delivering it to any person who will pay
the impoundment fee, together with all licensing costs, if any; or b) by
destroying the dog in a humane fashion.
   B.   Notice Of Impoundment:
      1.   Notice of impoundment shall be given to the owner by personal
service or by certified mail. Notice by certified mail shall be effective upon
mailing of same by City Clerk. In case of an unlicensed dog, notice of
impoundment shall be posted in an appropriate place on the front door of the
City Hall.
      2.   Failure to give notice as set forth in subsection B1 of this section
shall not prevent disposition of any impounded dog if the animal control
officer or his designee is unable, following inquiry, to ascertain the name or
location of the owner or persons having charge of the dog. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-
1990)
4-1A-8: DOGS SHOWING RABIES SYMPTOMS OR BITING ANY PERSON:
   A.   Authority: The animal control officer or his designee shall have the
authority to order the owner of any dog showing symptoms of rabies, or any dog
not having a rabies shot as attested by a current certificate of vaccination,
or of any dog which has bitten any person so as to cause an abrasion of the
skin to subject such dog to the City Pound for quarantine, for a period not to
exceed fifteen (15) days, and if such dog shall be determined free of rabies
the same shall be returned to the owner upon payment of one-half (1/2) of the
regular fee for keeping dogs impounded. No other fee shall be charged. If such
fee is not paid, the dog will be subject to disposal as hereinbefore provided.
   B.   Quarantine: However, in lieu of submitting such dog to the City Pound,
the animal control officer may, at the owner's expense, immediately admit such
dog to a veterinarian for examination, and said dog shall be quarantined with
the veterinarian until found not to have rabies.
   C.   Immediate Disposition: Any dog afflicted with rabies shall be disposed
of immediately, either by the owner or by the poundmaster. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-
1990)
4-1A-9: VICIOUS ANIMALS:
   A.   Definition; Exception:
      1.   Defined: A "vicious animal" is:
         a.   Any animal which, when unprovoked, in a taunting or terrorizing
manner, approaches any person in an apparent attitude of attack upon the
streets, sidewalks, any public grounds or places, or private property not owned
or possessed by the owner of the animal; or
         b.   Any animal with a known propensity, tendency, or disposition to
attack unprovoked, to cause injury, or to otherwise endanger the safety of
human beings or domestic animals; or
         c.   Any animal which bites, inflicts injury, assaults, or otherwise
attacks a human being or domestic animal without provocation; or
         d.   Any animal owned or harbored primarily or in part for the purpose
of fighting, or any animal trained for fighting; or
         e.   Any dog which has been trained as an attack dog, except dogs used
by law enforcement agencies.
      2.   Exception: Notwithstanding the above definition of a "vicious
animal", an animal is not necessarily vicious merely because injury or damage
is sustained by a person over the age of eighteen (18) who, at the time such
injury or damage was sustained, was committing a wilful trespass or other tort
upon the premises occupied by the owner of the animal, or was teasing,
tormenting, abusing, or assaulting the animal, or was committing or attempting
to commit a crime. An animal is not to be considered vicious if the animal was
protecting or defending a human being within the immediate vicinity of the
animal from an unjustified attack or assault.
   B.   Secure Enclosure: No owner or custodian shall keep a vicious animal
within the city limits unless such animal is kept within an absolutely secure
enclosure. A secure enclosure shall have a roof, a six foot (6') chainlink
fence, poles embedded in concrete footings extending one foot (1') belowground
and a concrete floor or foundation with the chainlink embedded three inches
(3") into the concrete.
   C.   Registration Required: Any person harboring, keeping or owning a
vicious animal shall register the animal with the city clerk.
   D.   Liability Insurance: Any person harboring, keeping or owning a vicious
animal which has not bitten any person on two (2) occasions, without
provocation, may continue to keep the animal upon posting with the city clerk a
liability insurance policy specifying not less than one hundred thousand
dollars ($100,000.00) liability for damages caused by the vicious animal and
further endorsing the city as party to be notified in the event of
cancellation.
   E.   Impound Or Dispose Of Animal; Failure To Comply: Any owner or custodian
whose animal has been reported to have bitten or attacked a human being on two
(2) occasions, without provocation, shall be required to give his or her animal
up for impoundment and disposal. Failure to comply with this section shall be a
misdemeanor and each day of failure to comply shall be separate violations of
this section.
   F.   Restraints Required: Any time the owner or custodian of a vicious
animal leaves the owner's or custodian's property the animal shall be
restrained with a chain and muzzle. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990)
4-1A-10: PENALTIES:
Any violation of this article shall constitute a misdemeanor punishable as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. Violation of subsection 4-1A-4A of this article shall be
punishable as set forth in subsection 4-1A-4B of this article which, if not
paid within ten (10) days, shall constitute a misdemeanor, punishable as set
forth in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 1990-2, 11-13-1990; amd. 1999 Code)
CHAPTER 2
MISCELLANEOUS OFFENSES
SECTION:
4-2-1: Discharging Firearms Or Fireworks
4-2-2: Fireworks; Explosives
4-2-3: Possession Or Consumption Of Intoxicating Substances In Public Places
4-2-1: DISCHARGING FIREARMS OR FIREWORKS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge any firearms or shoot off any
fireworks of any kind in the city; provided, however, that target practice may
be permitted if a proper backstop be placed behind the target, and no firearm
of greater than .22 caliber be used; and, provided further, that public
fireworks displays may be permitted by the city council upon public
celebrations. (1935 Code § 43; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
4-2-2: FIREWORKS; EXPLOSIVES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell, possess or give away any
firecrackers or any devices that depend upon the use of fire or flame in any
manner to operate them in the city, or to set off any explosives in the city,
for the purpose of amusement or celebration, nor shall any explosives be used
in the city unless the consent of the city council be first obtained. (1935
Code § 59; amd. Ord. 1, 8-1-1967)
4-2-3: POSSESSION OR CONSUMPTION OF INTOXICATING SUBSTANCES IN PUBLIC PLACES:
   A.   Unlawful: It shall be unlawful for any person to possess an open
container containing any alcoholic or other intoxicating substance, including
beer, or to consume any alcoholic or other intoxicating substance or beverage
of any kind, including beer, upon the streets, parks, public grounds, or
sidewalks, or in any public building, in the city.
   B.   Penalty: Any person convicted of violation of this section is guilty of
a misdemeanor and is punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. Each day a violation continues shall be considered a
separate offense. (Ord. 2001-2, 10-11-2001)
CHAPTER 3
JUNKED OR ABANDONED VEHICLES
SECTION:
4-3-1: Authority And Purpose
4-3-2: Definitions
4-3-3: Prohibition And Exceptions; Temporary Special Permit
4-3-4: Penalties, Civil Remedies, And Attorney Fees
4-3-1: AUTHORITY AND PURPOSE:
This chapter is adopted to promote the health, safety, and welfare of the
citizens of Franklin, and to promote a more aesthetically pleasing and healthy
environment. (Ord. 2011-6-8-2, 6-10-2011)
4-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
MOTOR VEHICLE: Any automobile, motorcycle, truck, trailer, semitrailer, truck
tractor and semitrailer combination, or other vehicle originally designed for
operation on the roads of this state, or any other state, or used to transport
persons or property, and propelled by power other than muscular power. Small
trailers, having less than ten thousand (10,000) pounds' gross vehicle weight,
which are used only for farming or agricultural purposes, shall not be
considered motor vehicles herein.
PERSON: Any individual, firm, partnership, trust, corporation, association, or
any group or organization or combination acting as a unit.
SIGHT OBSCURING: A fence, wall, or screen that is either solid or has openings
not to exceed twelve (12) square inches in every square foot. Further, the
sight obscuring structure must be at least six feet (6') high. (Ord. 2011-6-8-
2, 6-10-2011)
4-3-3: PROHIBITION AND EXCEPTIONS; TEMPORARY SPECIAL PERMIT:
   A.   No person shall store upon any area, lot, land, or parcel within
Franklin more than two (2) motor vehicles that are without current
registration, inoperable, or dismantled. Camp trailers shall be considered
registered if registered in the previous calendar year.
   B.   The prohibition contained herein shall not apply where the vehicles are
stored within a completely enclosed structure, or behind a sight obscuring
fence, wall, or screen.
   C.   Upon written application to the city, and with the approval of the city
council, which shall be granted for good cause shown, a person may receive a
temporary special permit to keep or store more than two (2) motor vehicles
which are not registered, are inoperable, or are dismantled. The approval
granted shall state the good cause for granting the permit, and shall specify
the terms and conditions of the special permit, including the time period by
which it will expire. (Ord. 2011-6-8-2, 6-10-2011)
4-3-4: PENALTIES, CIVIL REMEDIES, AND ATTORNEY FEES:
   A.   Any person in violation of this chapter shall first be given a written
notice of violation, which shall state the nature of the violation and set
forth the time period by which the violation must be abated. If the violation
is not abated within the prescribed time period, the city may proceed with
prosecution or a civil enforcement action.
   B.   Violation of this chapter is a misdemeanor, and punishable by a fine of
fifty dollars ($50.00) per day of violation, with the total fine not to exceed
three hundred dollars ($300.00) per year, and also by imprisonment of up to six
(6) months.
   C.   In addition to criminal enforcement of this chapter, Franklin may elect
to seek all civil and equitable remedies available at common law or under Idaho
law for the enforcement of this chapter. In the event that Franklin is the
prevailing party in any civil action involving enforcement of this chapter,
Franklin shall be awarded its reasonable costs and attorney fees. (Ord. 2011-6-
8-2, 6-10-2011)
TITLE 5
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
SECTION:
5-1-1: Adoption Of Idaho Motor Vehicle Laws
5-1-2: Parking Regulations
5-1-1: ADOPTION OF IDAHO MOTOR VEHICLE LAWS:
There is hereby adopted the motor vehicle laws of the state of Idaho, that
being particularly Idaho Code title 49, as presently in effect or as may
hereafter be amended, for the regulation of motor vehicles and motor vehicle
traffic within the city, and said Idaho motor vehicle laws, and any subsequent
amendments enacted into law by the Idaho legislature, contained in said
document, or its subsequent editions. (1999 Code)
5-1-2: PARKING REGULATIONS:
   A.   No Parking Areas: No vehicle shall be parked at any time, nor shall be
allowed to stand in any of the following places, except in compliance with
traffic control devices or at the direction of a police officer:
      1.   In any intersection.
      2.   In any crosswalk.
      3.   Within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant.
      4.   On any public sidewalk or parkway.
      5.   Any place where official signs prohibit parking.
      6.   Along any curb painted red. (Ord. 2007-9-11, 9-11-2007)
   B.   No Parking Zones:
      1.   U.S. Highway 91: No vehicle shall be parked at any time along the
road, curb, or right of way of U.S. Highway 91 at the following locations:
         a.   Along the west side of the highway between its intersection with
Main Street and a point one hundred twelve feet (112') south.
         b.   Along the east side of the highway between its intersection with
Main Street and a point thirty feet (30') south.
         c.   Along the east side of the highway between its intersection with
Main Street and a point one hundred sixty feet (160') north.
      2.   Main Street: No vehicle shall be parked at any time along the road,
curb, or road right of way of the city street known as Main Street at the
following locations:
         a.   Along the north side of said street between its intersection with
U.S. Highway 91 and a point sixty feet (60') west.
         b.   Along the south side of said street between its intersection with
U.S. Highway 91 and a point sixty feet (60') west.
         c.   Along the north side of said street between its intersection with
U.S. Highway 91 and a point thirty feet (30') east.
         d.   Along the south side of said street between its intersection with
U.S. Highway 91 and a point thirty feet (30') east. (Ord. 1991-1, 7-9-1991)
      3.   Overnight Parking Or Camping: No overnight parking or camping is
permitted around city parks or on city streets or rights of way, except out of
town family or friends may park in front of city residents' homes for a period
not to exceed seven (7) days, unless authorized by the mayor or a city
councilman. Violations are subject to towing at owner's expense and fine within
twenty four (24) hours.
      4.   Long Term Parking: No long term resident parking of cars, trucks,
tractors, trailers, boats, or recreational vehicles, on city rights of way
exceeding forty eight (48) hours. Violators will be warned and vehicles towed
at owners' expense and fined. Two (2) or more repeated offenses will be
prosecuted as a misdemeanor in the courts.
      5.   Miscellaneous Materials On Rights Of Way: No placement of
miscellaneous materials including, but not limited to, dirt, gravel, yard
clippings, limbs, etc., on city rights of way, exceeding a period of seventy
two (72) hours.
      6.   Short Term Parking: To ensure adequate parking, to permit sweeping
or snow removal, and to provide for public safety, a short term parking time
limit is provided to control parking of vehicles including trucks, trailers,
tractors, or farm equipment around city buildings, city parks or in city
provided parking areas. Parking will be limited to a maximum of four (4) hours
in a twenty four (24) hour period. This restriction excludes city employees
working at their assigned work locations; election workers and other scheduled
events such as family reunions, parties, and any event scheduled with the city
and approved by the city council or city employees. The parking provided at the
city parks is for those citizens using the parks and not for storing or selling
vehicles or for advertising or promoting private business or products.
Violators will be warned in writing. Failure to comply with this subsection
will result in a fine of twenty five dollars ($25.00) for the first offense;
and fifty dollars ($50.00) for each subsequent offense. The vehicle will be
towed or immobilized and all fines that are the responsibility of the
registered owner must be paid in full before the vehicle is released. (Ord., 9-
23-2004)
   C.   Parallel Parking: No vehicle shall be parked at any time along the
road, curb, or road right of way, except passenger cars by parking parallel to
said highway in a single row within eighteen inches (18") of the curb or barrow
pit, on the following streets or parts of streets:
      1.   U.S. Highway 91: Along the east side of U.S. Highway 91 between a
point thirty feet (30') south of the highway intersection with Main Street, and
a point one hundred seventeen feet (117') south therefrom.
      2.   Main Street: Along the south side of Main Street between a point
thirty feet (30') east of the street intersection with U.S. Highway 91, and a
point one hundred feet (100') eastward therefrom. (Ord. 1991-1, 7-9-1991)
   D.   Penalty: Any person violating any provision of this section shall be
guilty of a misdemeanor, and shall be subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 1991-1, 7-9-1991; amd. 1999 Code)
CHAPTER 2
STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND PUBLIC WAYS
SECTION:
5-2-1: Excavations
5-2-2: Obstructions
5-2-3: Water
5-2-4: Removal Of Snow, Ice And/Or Rubbish
5-2-5: Damages Or Construction
5-2-1: EXCAVATIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to tear up, damage, excavate, or make
inaccessible any sidewalk, public street, or alley of the city without first
getting the consent of the city council and posting an acceptable bond in an
amount approved by the city council or, if the council chooses to so delegate,
the director of public works. (Ord., 7-14-2010)
5-2-2: OBSTRUCTIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to place any obstructions including parking
vehicles, trailers, tractors, or any portion of these and other items that
block or partially block a public sidewalk or a public roadway. A courtesy
warning will be issued. Subsequent failure to comply and continuing to impede
the safe movement of pedestrians on any public sidewalks and any vehicular
traffic on any public roadways, or alleys within the city will be penalized
under provisions of section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord., 7-14-2010)
5-2-3: WATER:
   A.   Water Flowing On Public Ways: It shall be unlawful for any person using
or controlling water within the city, whether for irrigation or other use, to
permit the same to run upon any sidewalk or public street in the city.
   B.   Ditches Across Public Ways: It shall be unlawful for any person to
construct any ditches across any sidewalks or streets in the city without first
securing the consent of the city council, and placing a suitable box or culvert
under said sidewalk or street. (Ord., 7-14-2010)
5-2-4: REMOVAL OF SNOW, ICE AND/OR RUBBISH:
   A.   Snow, Ice And Rubbish: The owner, tenant or occupant of any premises
abutting or adjoining any sidewalk or alley within the city is hereby required
to remove all snow, ice and rubbish from said sidewalk and all rubbish from
said alley and to keep such sidewalk and alley clear of the same.
Owners, tenants, or homeowners' associations in any "PUDs", "subdivisions", or
"multiple-family developments" shall be required to remove all snow and ice
from all nondedicated streets, sidewalks, driveways and parking areas in such a
manner as to preclude damage or obstruction to any city streets or adjoining
property and to ensure access for city workers, agents and licensees.
   B.   Weeds, Grass And Rubbish: The owner, tenant or occupant of private
property within the city is required to and shall, within reason, keep such
premises free of weeds, rubbish, and unreasonably long grass, and shall
eradicate from such premises any diseases, pests, or vermin, including eggs and
larvae of any pests injurious to trees, plants, shrubs, or vines. This duty
extends from such private property to the center of any street or alley along
or in front of such property including parking within curbing abutting such
property.
   C.   Abatement By City: In the event the owner, tenant or occupant of any
premises or private property mentioned in subsection A or B of this section
shall fail to comply with the provisions of this section, the city shall have
the option, at its sole discretion, to remove such snow, ice and rubbish or cut
or remove such weeds, rubbish, and grass and assess the cost thereof against
the premises abutting the sidewalks or alleys so cleared or treated for
eradication and against the private property as cleaned or cleared or treated
for eradication. Such assessment shall be certified by the city clerk to the
county assessor or other proper county official having charge of making up the
assessment roll and such assessment shall be placed on the assessment roll and
collected in the same manner as other city taxes are collected. (Ord., 7-14-
2010)
5-2-5: DAMAGES OR CONSTRUCTION:
The city roads, right of way, curbs, and sidewalks are public assets hereafter
known as city assets in this section. Property owners and their agents
operating within the city of Franklin will be required to protect city assets
from damage. Prior to any landscaping, remodeling, repairs, or new construction
activity, the Franklin building inspector or the Franklin public works
department will certify the condition of the assets that may be affected by the
planned activity. The city may, at its option, require persons intending to
perform any landscaping, remodeling, repairs or new construction which impacts
the city assets, to post an acceptable bond in an appropriate amount as
determined by the city before any work begins. If damage occurs during the
construction, remodeling, landscaping, repair, or other improvement activities,
the owner or contractor is responsible for restoring the damaged asset to the
original condition and satisfaction of the city. If the necessary repairs are
not completed or, the city may, at its option, draw upon any bond so posted to
have the repairs completed or have the repairs completed and then bill the
owner. (Ord., 7-14-2010)
CHAPTER 3
WATER USE REGULATIONS
SECTION:
5-3-1: City Property
5-3-2: Duties Of Water Superintendent
5-3-3: Turning On, Shutting Off Water
5-3-4: Meters
5-3-5: Water Fees And Rates
5-3-6: Billing And Collection Of Water Rates
5-3-1: CITY PROPERTY:
All mains, laterals, pipes, hydrants and fixtures now laid, constructed or
installed or hereafter to be laid, constructed or installed, in, under, across
or through the streets, alleys and other thoroughfares of the city, or adjacent
territory, for supplying water to the city and the inhabitants thereof, are
hereby declared to be the property of the city under the control thereof and
subject to the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 20, 8-1-1978)
5-3-2: DUTIES OF WATER SUPERINTENDENT:
The water superintendent shall:
   A.   Have general supervision over the waterworks of the city, and
appurtenances thereto, under the direction of the mayor and city council.
   B.   Attend to the tapping of mains, laying and connecting laterals and
installation of meters and meter boxes. He shall see that all open ditches and
excavations on or along the streets, alleys and thoroughfares of the city are
carefully guarded by rails and lights or other proper warning signals.
   C.   Have charge of and operate the reservoir and keep the mains of said
system filled with pure and wholesome water at a pressure sufficient for proper
fire protection.
   D.   Keep an inventory of all property belonging to the water system and,
with the consent of the mayor and city council, purchase supplies and equipment
necessary for the maintenance of the system.
   E.   Upon request, attend meetings of the city council and render such
reports and statements as may be required of him by law or order of the mayor
and city council, and to the end that the provisions of this section may be
carried out, he shall be allowed such assistance as the mayor and city council
may deem necessary and proper. (Ord. 20, 8-1-1978)
5-3-3: TURNING ON, SHUTTING OFF WATER:
   A.   Authority: No water from the city water supply shall be turned on for
service into any premises by any person but the superintendent or some person
by him authorized to perform this service.
   B.   Application To Turn On Water: Application to have water turned on shall
be made by the owner of the property in writing to the clerk, and shall contain
an agreement by the applicant to abide by and accept all the provisions of this
chapter as conditions governing the use of the city water supply by the
applicant.
   C.   Plumbing Requirements: No water shall be turned on for service in
premises in which the plumbing does not comply with the specifications of the
city; provided, that water may be turned on for construction work in unfinished
buildings, subject to the provisions of this chapter.
   D.   Fee: The fee for disconnecting and reconnecting water hookups shall be
set by resolution. (Ord., 11-12-2014)
5-3-4: METERS:
   A.   Meters Required; Charges: All premises using city water must be
equipped with an adequate water meter which will be furnished by the city upon
payment of the following installation charges:
      1.   For residential type three-fourths inch (3/4") size meters, the fees
shall be set by resolution.
      2.   For commercial type meters of a size larger than three-fourths inch
(3/4") meter, the charges shall be determined by the mayor and the city
council.
   B.   Installation: All meters shall be installed under the direction of the
superintendent and subject to his approval.
   C.   Reading Meters:
      1.   The superintendent shall read or cause to be read every water meter
used in the city at such times as are necessary that the bills may be sent out
at the proper time.
      2.   The superintendent shall have access to any building at any
reasonable hour for the purpose of inspection of any part of the water system.
   D.   Testing Meters: Any city water meter shall be taken out and tested upon
complaint of the consumer, upon payment of a fee of ten dollars ($10.00). If
upon test the meter is not within three percent (3%) of being accurate, it
shall be repaired or replaced and the ten dollar ($10.00) fee returned to the
customer. (Ord., 11-12-2014)
5-3-5: WATER FEES AND RATES:
   A.   Any person or entity requesting a connection to the city culinary water
system must make application to the city clerk, pay the current water
connection fee as set by resolution of the city council, and, if the
application is approved and a connection is made, pay the monthly water rates
as set and amended from time to time by resolution of the city council.
   B.   Water connections will only be approved for a particular parcel of
property and are not transferable. (Ord. 2007-2-15, 2-15-2007)
5-3-6: BILLING AND COLLECTION OF WATER RATES:
   A.   Statements: Statements for water used shall be dated and sent out at
such times as specified by the mayor and city council.
   B.   Payment Of Bills; Discounts; Shutoff: The water supply may be shut off
from any premises for which the water bill remains unpaid for a period of
thirty (30) days after the bill is rendered and mailed. A discount shall be set
by resolution.
   C.   Charges A Lien:
      1.   Charges for water shall be a lien upon the premises as provided by
statute. Whenever a bill for water service remains unpaid sixty (60) days after
it has been rendered, the clerk may file with the recorder of the county a
statement of lien claim. This statement shall contain the legal description of
the premises served, the amount of the unpaid bill, and a notice that the city
claims a lien for this amount as well as for all charges for water served
subsequent to the period covered by the bill. If the consumer of water whose
bill is unpaid is not the owner of the premises, and the clerk has notice of
this, the notice shall be mailed to the owner of the premises, if his address
is known to the clerk, whenever such bill remains unpaid for a period of sixty
(60) days after it has been rendered.
      2.   The failure of the clerk to record such lien claim or to mail such
notice, or the failure of the owner to receive such notice, shall not affect
the right to foreclose the lien for unpaid water bills. (Ord., 11-12-2014)
ARTICLE A. CROSS-CONNECTIONS
SECTION:
5-3A-1: Purpose And Scope
5-3A-2: Definitions
5-3A-3: Cross-Connections Prohibited; Rules And Regulations
5-3A-4: Backflow Prevention Devices; Required
5-3A-5: Types Of Backflow Prevention Devices
5-3A-6: Installation Of Backflow Prevention Devices
5-3A-7: Underground Sprinkling Devices
5-3A-8: Installation Permits
5-3A-9: Inspections
5-3A-10: Additional Remedies
5-3A-11: Violation; Penalty
5-3A-1: PURPOSE AND SCOPE:
The purpose of this Article is to protect the public health of water consumers
by the control of actual and/or potential cross-connection. (Ord. 21, 9-2-1980)
5-3A-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this Article, terms used herein are defined as follows:
BACKFLOW: The flow, other than the intended direction of flow of any foreign
liquids, gases or substances into the distribution system of a public water
supply.
BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICE: A device to counteract back pressure or prevent
back siphonage.
CITY: The City of Franklin or its authorized agent.
CITY HEALTH OFFICER: The Health Officer of the City, or his authorized agent.
CONTAMINATION: The entry into or presence in public water supply of any
substance which may be deleterious to health and/or quality of the water.
CROSS-CONNECTION: Any physical arrangement whereby a public water supply is
connected, directly or indirectly, with any other water supply system, sewer,
