      7.   Required LID And BMP Selection: The City desires to "ensure that all
stormwater controls or management practices for new development and
redevelopment will prevent or minimize impacts to water quality. BMPs must be
selected that address pollutants known to be discharged or anticipated to be
discharged from site." As part of the selection of BMPs, the designer is to
evaluate and utilize LID methods that infiltrate, evapotranspire, or harvest
and use stormwater on site to protect water quality. The BMPs and procedures
included in this section summarize the design requirements for the most common
BMPs.
         a.   Mandatory LID Evaluation: Each project shall be evaluated for the
use of LID approach which encourages the implementation of BMPs that
infiltrate, evapotranspire or harvest and use stormwater on site to protect
water quality. The evaluation shall use and shall include both structural and
non-structural BMPs. If the designer determines that an LID approach cannot be
utilized, the designer shall document and explain the reasons that LID will not
work on the specific site and provide the rationale for the chosen alternative
controls that will be used to obtain the same water quality objectives. This
evaluation shall be completed on a case by case basis. As a minimum, the
evaluation shall document:
            (1)   Why LID will not work.
            (2)   Rationale for the chosen alternative controls on a case by
case basis for each project.
         b.   Mandatory LID Included On All Projects:
            (1)   Development In Riparian Areas:
               (A)   Riparian areas are defined as being within seventy five
feet (75') of centerline of stream drainage a basin larger than one square
mile, and land within twenty five feet (25') of stream centerline for streams
that drain areas of one square mile or less.
               (B)   All structures shall maintain a setback of twenty five
feet (25') from the top of the stream bank within a riparian area.
               (C)   No more than fifty percent (50%) of the land area within
the riparian area may be disturbed, including grading, clearing, grubbing, tree
removal, etc. All disturbed areas shall be revegetated within sixty (60) days
of initial disturbance.
               (D)   Trees larger than twelve inches (12") dbh shall not be
removed from the riparian area unless they are considered a hazard tree,
diseased or dead.
            (2)   Open Space Preservation:
               (A)   Open space is an area of land or water that may be used
for passive or active recreation, agriculture, conservation, landscaped areas,
preservation of the natural environment, scenic land, and/or other similar
uses.
               (B)   Minimum open space by development type shall include:
                  (i) Residential: Twenty percent (20%).
                  (ii) Commercial: Ten percent (10%).
                  (iii) Industrial: Ten percent (10%).
               (C)   A permanent restrictive covenant in the form of a
perpetual conservation easement shall be placed upon open space land requiring
its maintenance as open space.
            (3)   Land Designation As A Resource Conservation Zone:
               (A)   The Resource Conservation Zone includes lands protected
from development such as highly productive agricultural lands, areas of high
visual value, and critical environmental resources especially including lands
critical to protecting the water quality of our rivers and streams. Much of
this land would be wetlands.
               (B)   This zone is intended to maintain the vegetation in this
area.
            (4)   Landscaping:
               (A)   Refer to the City's Development Code.
         c.   Infiltration BMPs:
            (1)   At Grade Retention/Infiltration Basins:
               (A)   All retention basins shall be sized to meet the
requirements of this section and to contain one hundred percent (100%) of
project site runoff from the design storm.
               (B)   Side slopes shall not be steeper than 3:1 (H:V).
               (C)   The maximum depth of the pond shall be three feet (3')
plus one foot (1') of freeboard above the emergency overflow and a maximum
water depth of three feet (3') below the emergency overflow. All other ponds
require special design, approval, and permitting including safety precautions
on a case by case situation.
               (D)   All ponds shall be stabilized with rocks or planted
vegetation to prevent internal erosion. Vegetation or other stabilization shall
be maintained.
               (E)   All ponds shall drain within three (3) days (72 hours)
from the end of the storm event. This is to be documented with a certified
percolation test of the native sub-grade material and the material placed
during construction, and documented in the soils report.
               (F)   Emergency overflows and the flow path of the overflows
shall be mapped for purpose of flooding.
               (G)   The emergency overflow shall be designed to pass the full
100-year event.
               (H)   Other utilities (for example water lines, sewer lines, gas
lines, power lines, phone lines, etc.) shall not be allowed through the
retention pond or within five feet (5') of the pond berms.
               (I)   The invert or lowest point in the pond shall be not less
than twelve inches (12") above the historically highest groundwater levels.
               (J)   The bottom of the pond shall be finished to maintain
historical infiltration.
            (2)   Underground Retention/Infiltration Systems:
               (A)   Underground buried retention and injections systems are
not allowed in Drinking Water Source Protection Zones 1 and 2.
               (B)   Underground systems shall provide adequate access points
for cleaning and maintenance of the underground chambers.
               (C)   All systems shall drain by infiltration within three (3)
days (72 hours) from the end of the storm event. This is to be documented with
a certified percolation test and documented in the soils report.
               (D)   Sumps shall provide adequate water quality treatment to
prevent contamination of the groundwater aquifer.
               (E)   Emergency overflows and the flow path of the overflows
shall be mapped for purpose of flooding and flood insurance requirements.
               (F)   The emergency overflow shall be designed to pass the full
100-year event.
               (G)   Other utilities (for example water lines, sewer lines, gas
lines, power lines, phone lines, etc.) shall not be allowed through or under
the underground retention system.
               (H)   Registration with the DEQ of a Class 5 injection well
permit are required for all underground retention/infiltration systems.
            (3)   Infiltration Trenches:
               (A)   Infiltration trenches are not allowed in Drinking Water
Source Protection Zones 1 and 2.
               (B)   Infiltration trenches shall provide adequate access points
for cleaning and maintenance underground piping.
               (C)   Infiltration trenches shall drain by infiltration within
three (3) days (72 hours) from the end of the storm event to provide adequate
storage for a subsequent event. This is to be documented with a certified
percolation test and documented in the soils report.
               (D)   Infiltration trenches shall have adequate water quality
treatment to prevent contamination of the groundwater aquifer.
               (E)   Emergency overflows and the flow path of the overflows
shall be mapped for purpose of flooding and flood insurance requirements.
               (F)   The emergency overflow shall be designed to pass the full
100-year event.
               (G)   Other utilities (for example water lines, sewer lines, gas
lines, power lines, phone lines, etc.) shall not be allowed through or under
the infiltration trenches.
               (H)   Registration of Class 5 injections well permits are
required for all infiltration trenches.
            (4)   Infiltration Swales:
               (A)   Side slopes shall not be steeper than 4:1 (H:V).
               (B)   The maximum depth of the pond shall be one foot (1').
               (C)   All ponds shall be landscaped per landscaping
requirements. Vegetation or other stabilization shall be maintained.
               (D)   All swales shall drain within three (3) days (72 hours)
from the end of the storm event. This is to be documented with a certified
percolation test of the native sub-grade material and the material placed
during construction and documented in the soils report.
               (E)   Emergency overflows and the flow path of the overflows
shall be mapped for purpose of flooding to ensure all emergency overflows are
to the PWD drainage system.
               (F)   The invert or lowest point in the pond shall be not less
than twelve inches (12") above the historically highest groundwater levels.
               (G)   The bottom of the pond shall be finished to maintain
historical infiltration.
            (5)   Permeable Pavements: Permeable (or pervious) pavements
contain small voids that allow water to pass through to a stone base. They come
in a variety of forms; they may be modular paving system (concrete pavers,
modular grass or gravel grids) or poured in place pavement (porous concrete,
permeable asphalt). All permeable pavements with a stone reservoir base treat
stormwater to remove sediments and metals to some degree by allowing stormwater
to percolate through the pavement and enter the soil below. All permeable
pavement systems shall be designed to ensure that water in the pavement and the
rocks below completely infiltrate into the soil within seventy two (72) hours.
            (6)   Injection Wells (Sumps):
               (A)   Injection wells also known as sumps are not allowed in
Drinking Water Source Protection Zones 1 and 2.
               (B)   Injection wells shall provide adequate access points for
cleaning and maintenance underground piping.
               (C)   Injection wells shall drain by infiltration within three
(3) days (72 hours) from the end of the storm event to provide adequate storage
for a subsequent event. This is to be documented with a certified percolation
test and documented in the soils report.
               (D)   Injection wells shall have adequate water quality
treatment to prevent contamination of the groundwater aquifer.
               (E)   Emergency overflows and the flow path of the overflows
shall be mapped for purpose of flooding and flood insurance requirements.
               (F)   The emergency overflow shall be designed to pass the full
100-year event.
               (G)   Registration of Class 5 injections well permits are
required for all infiltration trenches.
         d.   Stormwater Harvesting:
            (1)   The stormwater harvesting will be reviewed by the City and
DEQ on a case by case basis.
         e.   Natural Filters: Natural filter facilities are landscaped shallow
depressions that capture and filter stormwater runoff. As stormwater passes
down through the planting soil, pollutants are filtered, adsorbed, and
biodegraded by the soil and plants. Because they are not contained within an
impermeable structure, they may allow for infiltration.
Projects that have demonstrated they cannot manage one hundred percent (100%)
of the water quality design volume onsite through infiltration and/or
stormwater harvesting BMPs may manage the remaining volume through the use of a
high removal efficiency natural filter BMP. A high removal efficiency natural
filter BMP shall be sized to adequately capture 1.5 times the volume not
managed through infiltration and/or capture and use.
            (1)   Bio-Filters: Most natural filter systems can be classified as
biofilters. They normally consist of a ponding area, mulch layer, planting
soils, plants, and in some cases an underdrain. Runoff that passes through a
biofiltration system is treated by the natural absorption and filtration
characteristics of the plants, soils, and microbes with which the water
contacts.
            (2)   Rain Gardens: Rain gardens are simply gardens designed to
capture and treat runoff. They are generally small in size and should not be
used to treat impervious areas exceeding four thousand (4,000) square feet.
Rain gardens most often utilize native plant species and soil amendments to
encourage absorption of stormwater. For projects with impervious areas
exceeding four thousand (4,000) square feet biofilters, planter boxes with
infiltration, vegetated swales or natural buffer strips should be considered.
            (3)   Planter Boxes With Infiltration: Planter boxes with
infiltration are natural filtration treatment control measures located in and
around structures and facilities to handle larger volumes of water than a
typical rain garden. They typically are constructed with vertical or near
vertical sides and above ground. They can be equipped with underdrains if
necessary. Planter boxes with infiltration should maintain setbacks from
adjacent buildings, other structures, sidewalks or roadways.
            (4)   Vegetated Swales: Vegetated swales are open, shallow channels
with dense, low-lying vegetation covering the side slopes and bottom that
collect and slowly convey runoff to downstream discharge points. An effective
vegetated swale achieves uniform sheet flow through the densely vegetated area
for a period of several minutes. The vegetation in the swale can vary depending
on its location and is the choice of the designer. Most swales are grass-lined.
            (5)   Filter Or Buffer Strips: Filter strips are vegetated areas
designed to treat sheet flow runoff from adjacent impervious surfaces such as
parking lots and roadways, or intensive landscaped areas such as golf courses.
While some assimilation of dissolved constituents may occur, filter strips are
generally more effective in trapping sediment and particulate-bound metals,
nutrients, and pesticides. Filter strips are more effective when the runoff
passes through the vegetation and thatch layer in the form of shallow, uniform
flow. Filter strips are primarily used to pretreat runoff before it flows to an
infiltration BMP or another natural filtration BMP.
         f.   Man-Made Treatment:
            (1)   Planter Boxes: Planter boxes are bioretention treatment
control measures that are completely contained within an impermeable structure
with an underdrain (they do not infiltrate). They are similar to bioretention
facilities with underdrains except they are situated at or above ground and are
bound by impermeable walls. Planter boxes may be placed adjacent to or near
buildings, other structures, or sidewalks.
            (2)   Hydrodynamic Separators: Hydrodynamic separators are
stormwater management devices that work primarily based on vortex and gravity
principles to separate stormwater from the pollutants. They are generally
designed as flow-through systems with either on-line or off-line storage of
pollutants. They include chambers for settling and storage of pollutants and
are often used in conjunction with other BMPs as pretreatment. They are not
especially effective for the removal of fine materials or dissolved pollutants.
On-line separators are more susceptible to scour or re-suspension of pollutants
than systems that incorporate off-line storage.
         g.   Settlement Systems: Settlement systems are used to store and
settle out sediment using Stokes Law. This approach does not infiltrate,
harvest, or evaporate sufficient water. However, it can be used in combination
with other BMPs to ensure treatment of water above the 90th percentile storm to
ensure water quality requirements and the flow requirements of the canal
companies are met.
            (1)   At Grade Detention Basins:
               (A)   Side slopes shall not be steeper than 3:1 (H:V).
               (B)   The maximum depth at the emergency overflow location of
the pond shall be three feet (3') plus one foot (1') of freeboard above the
emergency overflow and a maximum water depth of three feet (3') below the
emergency overflow. All other ponds require special design, approval, and
permitting including safety precautions on a case by case situation.
               (C)   All ponds shall be stabilized with rocks or planted
vegetation to prevent internal erosion. Vegetation or other stabilization must
be maintained.
               (D)   Where orifice and snouts are used, the orifice size is
limited to not less than three inches (3") in diameter to prevent clogging.
               (E)   Emergency overflows and the flow path of the overflows
shall be mapped to natural streams, canals, or City approved drainage system
for purpose of flood mapping using existing topographic mapping.
               (F)   The emergency overflow shall be designed to pass the full
100-year event.
               (G)   Other utilities (for example water lines, sewer lines, gas
lines, power lines, phone lines, etc.) shall not be allowed through the
detention pond or within five feet (5') of the pond berms.
               (H)   The invert or lowest point in the pond shall be not less
than twelve inches (12") above the historically highest groundwater levels
(whichever is higher).
               (I)   The bottom of the pond shall be finished to maintain
historical infiltration.
            (2)   Underground Detention Systems:
               (A)   Underground systems shall provide adequate access points
for cleaning and maintenance.
               (B)   All detention systems shall drain by discharge (detention
basins) within three (3) days (72 hours) from the end of the storm event. This
is to be documented.
               (C)   Emergency overflows and the flow path of the overflows
shall be mapped for purpose of flooding and flood insurance requirements.
               (D)   The emergency overflow shall be designed to pass the full
100-year event.
               (E)   Other utilities (for example water lines, sewer lines, gas
lines, power lines, phone lines, etc.) shall not be allowed through or under
the underground retention system.
      8.   Curb And Gutter Flow Design:
         a.   The flow depth in the gutter shall not be allowed to exceed the
lesser of the top back of curb elevation (TBC) or the peak drive way approach
elevation during the required storm event. This includes a combination of
piping, curb and gutter, and ditches.
         b.   Where the flow depth is exceeded, storm drain inlets and a piped
system shall be required and appropriate actions taken to eliminate overtopping
of the curbs and flooding private property.
      9.   Channel Design:
         a.   Channel side slopes shall not be steeper than 3:1 (H:V) unless
they are concrete. Where they are incorporated into landscaping, flatter slopes
shall be required. This will be evaluated on a case by case basis.
         b.   Channel velocities shall be slow enough to prevent scour, and
where possible, facilitate further settlement of sediments unless the channel
is used to deliver irrigation water as well. If the channel will also carry
irrigation water, maintain velocities above two feet (2') per second if
possible, but at no time exceed four feet (4') per second.
         c.   Where rip-rap is used, design shall be in accordance with EM-1110
from the U.S. Army Corp of Engineers or HEC-11 from the Federal Highway
Administration.
         d.   Freeboard on the channels shall be in compliance with the Bureau
of Reclamation, Design of Small Canal Structures.
         e.   Channel maintenance easements shall be maintained as required in
the City and canal company agreements.
      10.   Pipe Design:
         a.   For stormwater pipes, roughness coefficients listed in the table
included in section
5-5-5 of this chapter that coincide with the accepted pipe materials in the
City's Standard Specifications, most current edition shall be used.
         b.   Maintain velocities in the pipes at design flows sufficient to
prevent sediment deposition and low enough to prevent scour damage to the pipe.
         c.   Pipe outlets shall have a flared end discharge unless more
stringent methods of energy dissipation are required.
         d.   Minimum diameter of storm drains shall be:
            (1)   Twelve inches (12") for laterals;
            (2)   Fifteen inches (15") for trunk lines;
            (3)   Eighteen inches (18") under the ITD right-of-way.
         e.   Pipe sizes shall not decrease in the downstream direction.
         f.   Maximum flow depth in the pipe during the design storm shall not
exceed 0.85 times the diameter of the pipe. (Res. 2019-5-08, 5-8-2019, eff. 5-
8-2019)
5-5-4: REQUIRED HYDROLOGIC METHODOLOGY:
   A.   Methods And Procedures:
      1.   Design Methodology: The following table summarizes the required
methods based on the area contributing flows to the system, including offsite
flows. The rational equation is not allowed for design of Best Management
Practices.
   HYDROLOGIC METHODS REQUIRED

      2.   Design Hyetographs: The following table summarizes the hyetograph
which shall be used during the design.
   REQUIRED DESIGN HYETOGRAPH

      3.   Hydrologic Procedures: The SCS method, as developed in TR-55 by the
Soil Conservation Service in the 1950s, requires the designer to address the
soil conditions, vegetative cover, and the antecedent soil condition (AMC)
being evaluated.
         a.   SCS Soil Conditions: Soil maps and references available from the
Natural Resource Conservation Service will identify the group associated with
each soil class. However, the designer needs to consider the effects of the
final landscaping, such as the use of top soil, as part of his design.
There are four (4) primary soil conditions available in the SCS method, grouped
as A, B, C, and D.
Group A soils typically are gravels and sands with fast infiltration rates and
low runoff potential. While there are group A soils on some of the benches and
along the rivers in some places, as soon as any landscaping with topsoil
occurs, the stormwater benefit is lost. Unless specific LID design is
incorporated to maintain the infiltration potential of these soils, final
landscaping will require a different soil group.
Group B soils have moderate infiltration rates when wetted and consist of
moderately well drained soils with moderately fine to coarse textures,
typically without clay.
Group C soils have slow infiltration rates if thoroughly wetted and consist of
soils that have a layer that impedes vertical infiltration.
Group D soils have a slow infiltration rate if thoroughly wetted and consist of
clays, usually with high swelling potential, soils with a permanent high-water
table, soils with a clay pan or hard pan layer near the surface, and shallow
soils over an impervious material.
         b.   Antecedent Soil Conditions: In addition to the soil group, the
antecedent moisture condition (AMC) must also be considered. For the average
case, the SCS has defined AMC II to apply as the definition of the conditions
preceding most annual floods. For this purpose, AMC II will be used for all PWD
approved projects.
Upon selecting the soil group, the appropriate curve number can be selected
from various standard references and text books. A common free reference is the
HEC-HMS Technical Reference Manual which can be downloaded from the Army Corp
of Engineers HEC website. Runoff coefficients are subject to approval by the
City Engineer.
         c.   Runoff Coefficients: PWD has established standard runoff
coefficients that shall be used to ensure compatibility of results from the
base model and each individual project. Calculations differing from these
values shall be returned to the design professional for corrections.
   REQUIRED RUNOFF COEFFICIENT (CN)

cover >75%)

       1.    Where the weighted values are too cumbersome to calculate, or
insufficient data is available outside of the project area, use these values.
         d.   Time Of Concentrations Calculations: There are numerous equations
for calculating the time of concentrations. While many may be applicable to
various locations, the following table identifies the methods that shall be
used in determining the time of concentrations within the PWD areas.

5-5-5: HYDRAULIC CALCULATIONS:
   A.   Hydraulic calculations shall be used for sizing pipes and open channels
associated with the total design flows.
      1.   Channel Design: Channels shall be designed with a trapezoidal cross
section using roughness coefficients associated with the final restored
condition. The Manning's equation methodology shall be used for sizing and
considering the associated backwater impacts from downstream conditions.
Computer software can be used to calculate the channel size, but sufficient
data and results shall be provided to validate the procedure, assumptions, and
conclusions.
      2.   Pipe Design: For design of pipes and culverts, the designer shall
demonstrate that the pipes meet the standard design requirements using
Manning's equation for open channel flow and standard culvert calculation
procedures to determine inlet and outlet control conditions. Full pipe flow
designs are not allowed for gravity systems. For stormwater pressure mains from
pump stations, either the Hazen-Williams or Darcy-Weisbach equations will be
allowed. Roughness coefficients and assumptions shall be in accordance with the
following table selected from various references.
   MANNINGS COEFFICIENTS FOR PIPE
 
Material                         Roughness "n"
Smooth interior HDPE or ADS pipe 0.010
Corrugated metal pipe (CMP)      0.024
Concrete                         0.013
PVC                              0.010
 
The design and sizing may be done manually or with the use of computer
software. However, the results must be provided as part of the submittal review
process.
      3.   Spread Width Calculations: Spread width calculations and depth of
flow in the gutters shall be completed in accordance with HEC-22 methodology
developed by the Federal Highway Administration (FHWA). These calculations can
be completed using numerous available software or manually. However, the
calculations must be documented and provided to the City for review for the
design storms.
(Res. 2019-5-08, 5-8-2019, eff. 5-8-2019)
CHAPTER 6
PUBLICLY OWNED TREATMENT WORKS (POTW) PRETREATMENT PROGRAM
SECTION:
5-6-1: Purpose And Scope
5-6-2: Definitions
5-6-3: Legal Authority And Enforcement
5-6-3-1: Legal Authority
5-6-3-2: Control Mechanisms
5-6-3-3: General Control Mechanisms For Similar Industrial Users
5-6-3-4: Monitoring And Inspection
5-6-4: Enforcement And Penalties
5-6-4-1: Remedies For Non-Compliance
5-6-4-2: Confidentiality
5-6-5: Industrial User Reporting Requirements
5-6-5-1: Reporting Obligations
5-6-6: Water Sampling Requirements
5-6-1: PURPOSE AND SCOPE:
   This Chapter establishes the legal authority for the City of Franklin,
Idaho, to implement and enforce a Pretreatment Program for the Publicly Owned
Treatment Works (POTW), consistent with sections 307(b), 307(c), and 402(b)(8)
and (9) of the Clean Water Act and the regulations outlined in 40 CFR 403. The
purpose is to regulate the discharge of pollutants into the POTW to protect the
wastewater treatment process, ensure compliance with the National Pollutant
Discharge Elimination System (NPDES) permit, and prevent harm to human health,
property, and the environment.
(Ord. 2024-11-13, 11-13-2024)
5-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
   The following definitions apply to terms used in this Chapter:
   POTW: The Publicly Owned Treatment Works owned and operated by the City of
Franklin, Idaho.
   INDUSTRIAL USER (IU): A source of indirect discharge that introduces
pollutants into the POTW from a non-domestic source.
   SIGNIFICANT INDUSTRIAL USER (SIU): Any industrial user that meets the
criteria defined under 40 CFR 403.3(v).
   PRETREATMENT STANDARDS: The standards under Section 307(b) and (c) of the
Clean Water Act, including both categorical and local limits.
(Ord. 2024-11-13, 11-13-2024)
5-6-3: LEGAL AUTHORITY AND ENFORCEMENT:
5-6-3-1: LEGAL AUTHORITY:
   The City of Franklin, Idaho, shall operate under the authority provided by
Federal, State, and local law to implement and enforce all pretreatment
requirements of the Clean Water Act and 40 CFR 403. This includes the authority
to:
   A.   Deny or condition new or increased contributions of pollutants to the
POTW by industrial users that do not meet applicable Pretreatment Standards or
cause violations of the POTW’s NPDES permit.
   B.   Require compliance by industrial users with all applicable Pretreatment
Standards and Requirements.
   C.   Issue individual or general control mechanisms (permits, orders, or
equivalent) for the contribution of pollutants by significant industrial users
to ensure compliance.
   D.   Require industrial users to develop compliance schedules and submit
required reports and monitoring data to demonstrate adherence to pretreatment
standards.
   E.   Inspect, monitor, and enter any industrial premises as necessary to
ensure compliance.
   F.   Obtain remedies for non-compliance, including injunctive relief, civil,
or criminal penalties of at least $1,000 per day per violation.
   G.   Ensure confidentiality of any proprietary information, consistent with
40 CFR 403.14.
(Ord. 2024-11-13, 11-13-2024)
5-6-3-2: CONTROL MECHANISMS:
   For industrial users, the POTW shall issue control mechanisms that are
enforceable and contain, at a minimum:
   A.   A statement of the control mechanism’s duration (not to exceed five
years).
   B.   Conditions of non-transferability without prior notice and provision of
a copy of the existing mechanism to any new owner/operator.
   C.   Effluent limits and Best Management Practices based on general
Pretreatment Standards, local limits, and state and federal law.
   D.   Self-monitoring, sampling, and reporting requirements, identifying the
pollutants to be monitored, sampling locations, and frequency.
   E.   Civil and criminal penalties for violations, along with any applicable
compliance schedules.
   F.   Provisions for controlling Slug Discharges, if deemed necessary by the
POTW.
(Ord. 2024-11-13, 11-13-2024)
5-6-3-3: GENERAL CONTROL MECHANISMS FOR SIMILAR INDUSTRIAL USERS:
   At the POTW’s discretion, significant industrial users with similar
operations, discharge types, and effluent limits may be subject to a general
control mechanism, provided they meet the following conditions:
   A.   AU facilities involved must discharge similar types of waste and
require similar effluent limitations and monitoring.
   B.   The significant industrial user must file a written request for
coverage under the general control mechanism, including details of production
processes, waste monitoring, and requests for any monitoring waivers.
(Ord. 2024-11-13, 11-13-2024)
5-6-3-4: MONITORING AND INSPECTION:
   The POTW shall establish procedures to:
   A.   Monitor industrial discharges, including the authority to enter
industrial premises, inspect facilities, and access records as required under
Section 308 of the Clean Water Act.
   B.   Conduct surveillance and sampling independently of industrial users to
verify compliance with Pretreatment Standards.
(Ord. 2024-11-13, 11-13-2024)
5-6-4: ENFORCEMENT AND PENALTIES:
5-6-4-1: REMEDIES FOR NON-COMPLIANCE:
   In the event of non-compliance with any applicable Pretreatment Standards or
requirements, the City of Franklin, Idaho, shall have the authority to:
   A.   Seek injunctive relief, enforce civil and criminal penalties, or both,
in amounts not less than $1,000 per violation per day.
   B.   Immediately halt any discharge that presents an imminent threat to
human health, safety, or the environment.
   C.   Halt any discharge that may interfere with the POTW’s operations or
result in environmental endangerment.
(Ord. 2024-11-13, 11-13-2024)
5-6-4-2: CONFIDENTIALITY:
   A.   The City of Franklin, Idaho, shall maintain the confidentiality of
industrial user information, particularly trade secrets and proprietary data,
in compliance with 40 CFR 403.14.
   B.   Disclosure of such information shall be limited to regulatory
authorities as required.
(Ord. 2024-11-13, 11-13-2024)
5-6-5: INDUSTRIAL USER REPORTING REQUIREMENTS:
5-6-5-1: REPORTING OBLIGATIONS:
   Industrial users must submit all reports necessary to assess compliance with
applicable Pretreatment Standards, including but not limited to:
   A.   Baseline monitoring reports.
   B.   Compliance schedule progress reports.
   C.   Periodic compliance reports, including self-monitoring data, as
required under 40 CFR403.12.
(Ord. 2024-11-13, 11-13-2024)
5-6-6: WATER SAMPLING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Sampling for Significant Industrial Users (SIUs):
      1.   Frequency: SIUs must conduct water sampling at least twice per year
(semi-annually) or more frequently as specified in their individual or general
control mechanisms, depending on the nature of the discharge.
      2.   Sampling Location: All samples must be taken at a designated
compliance sampling point prior to the discharge entering the POTW but after
treatment processes at the industrial facility.
      3.   Sample Type: Sampling must include both composite samples (collected
over a period of time) and grab samples (single samples taken at a specific
time) to capture a representative profile of the discharge.
   B.   Sampling for Contaminants: The following contaminants must be monitored
for industrial users, and the corresponding allowable concentrations (which
shall not be exceeded) are provided below. Local limits must be revised as
necessary to comply with NPDES permit requirements and state regulations.
Contaminant Allowable Concentration (mg/L) Sampling Method
Contaminant                      Allowable Concentration (mg/L) Sampling Method
Biochemical Oxygen Demand (BOD5) 300 mg/L (local limit)         Composite
Total Suspended Solids (TSS)     350 mg/L (local limit)         Composite
pH                               6.0 to 9.0 SU (standard units) Grab
Oil and Grease                   100 mg/L                       Grab
Ammonia (as N)                   20 mg/L (local limit)          Composite
Total Phosphorus                 10 mg/L (local limit)          Composite
Arsenic                          0.10 mg/L                      Grab
Cadmium                          0.05 mg/L                      Grab
